    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_38358417" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38358417" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/289897-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583165983p2/289897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38358417?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/289897-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289897-kristen?shelf=medievalism">medievalism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289897-kristen?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289897-kristen?shelf=irish">irish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289897-kristen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289897-kristen?shelf=paganism">paganism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289897-kristen?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer38358417&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38358417" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17195465076310999202">EDIT: I just reread this and enjoyed it much more than I apparently did the first time. I say apparently because, oddly, I have absolutely no recollection of reading this book previously. That almost never happens to me. Once I read a story, I tend to remember them. Anyway, I definitely liked this a great deal. I am also stoked about reading the next book in the Sevenwaters series as well as the new book Marillier has coming out this fall!<br/><br/>**Old review**<br/>As far as Juliet Marillier's books go, this</span>
  <span id="freeText17195465076310999202" style="display:none">EDIT: I just reread this and enjoyed it much more than I apparently did the first time. I say apparently because, oddly, I have absolutely no recollection of reading this book previously. That almost never happens to me. Once I read a story, I tend to remember them. Anyway, I definitely liked this a great deal. I am also stoked about reading the next book in the Sevenwaters series as well as the new book Marillier has coming out this fall!<br /><br />**Old review**<br />As far as Juliet Marillier's books go, this was fairly sub-standard. While the previous three Sevenwaters books had a similar trait--the sheltered young woman leaves home for various reasons and falls in love with a young man who would otherwise be completely unacceptable were it not for his honor/loyalty/save something at the last minute--this one was too formulaic. I think Marillier can do much better. That said, this was still a wonderful book and Marillier is a better writer than many out there. <br /><br />I did like that this one was more "Otherworldly" than the others. The others all had elements of the Otherworld, this one was largely set in the land of Faerie. It was a much darker book than many of Marillier's usual, which I really liked, actually. Yes, the lovers still end up married happily, but there is a shadow hanging over them. There is ample room for another Sevenwaters book, and I do hope that it Marillier's intent. I still enjoy her writing immensely, even when I think she could do better, as here. <br /><br />Anyway, I also liked that Clodagh was not a typical heroine. In fact, she was nothing more than a girl who was more than capable of running a large household, not much more, as was noted more than once throughout the book. But she overcomes her fears and self doubt to save her lover at great personal risk. In that regard, she is typical of the female hero. But she didn't have the same sense of confidence that the three previous women had. Even Fainne, in <i>Child of the Prophecy</i> had a bit more confidence. Clodagh knew what she had to do and didn't hesitate to do it, but she had fears the whole time. In that regard, she was probably more realistic than any of the others, including Fainne. <br /><br />At the end of the day, this was a book about selfless love, many, many different kinds. It would be good book for younger readers as well as adults. It can stand alone from the other Sevenwaters books, which is nice. Everything that is mentioned from the other books is easily explained in a way that's not annoying for those who've read the previous books but is sufficient for those who haven't to understand what's happening. <br /><br />Overall, this is still a very good book, and I would recommend it to fantasy fans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17195465076310999202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer47492717&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47492717" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4123821951499278039">Extremely disappointing. I can't believe the same person wrote this and the first two books of the Sevenwaters trilogy. "Daughter of the Forrest" and "Son of the Shadows" were amazing - seriously two of my favorite books. But "Heir to Sevenwaters" was a complete let down! Marilier didn't develop the characters (or maybe I think that because I never really connected with them). The plot had a good premise, but she could have done better. And the heroine was nothing special. And there were pages o</span>
  <span id="freeText4123821951499278039" style="display:none">Extremely disappointing. I can't believe the same person wrote this and the first two books of the Sevenwaters trilogy. "Daughter of the Forrest" and "Son of the Shadows" were amazing - seriously two of my favorite books. But "Heir to Sevenwaters" was a complete let down! Marilier didn't develop the characters (or maybe I think that because I never really connected with them). The plot had a good premise, but she could have done better. And the heroine was nothing special. And there were pages of the main characters professing their love over and over. I would say it would be a good teen book except for their fascination with wanting (and the ability) to have sex together. Plus, give me a break... Johnny can't be gay! Is Marillier just trying to normalize homosexuality or is she just jumping on the current pro-gay bandwagon? Not a fan of this book. She set the story up for more books, but if they are anything like Heir to Sevenwaters I would rather not read them. I like my own imagined endings for these stories better. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="4123821951499278039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4649093-katie-mcsweeney?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer493993602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16440179478771637989">Not anywhere near as good as the other three Sevenwaters books...<br/><br/> I was very disappointed by Clodagh's character she wasn't the sort of heroine that I was expecting. She said that she was only suited to housework but then she outdid herself and succeeded on her quest... perfect start for a heroine! <br/><br/>...But then she found a boy she fancied and became 100% self-sacrificing for her love... she went so far as to suggest that she could have come up with a way to get out of the Otherworld but that she </span>
  <span id="freeText16440179478771637989" style="display:none">Not anywhere near as good as the other three Sevenwaters books...<br /><br /> I was very disappointed by Clodagh's character she wasn't the sort of heroine that I was expecting. She said that she was only suited to housework but then she outdid herself and succeeded on her quest... perfect start for a heroine! <br /><br />...But then she found a boy she fancied and became 100% self-sacrificing for her love... she went so far as to suggest that she could have come up with a way to get out of the Otherworld but that she needed to let Cathal find his own way out for the sake of his manly pride. She does something extraordinary even though she is very ordinary. That is not the type of human heroism i was anticipating. I was disappointed that within days she was willing to risk her life for the sake of his pride. Though he seems lovely and I can imagine a happy ending for them, I just wish that Clodagh had more gumption!!<br /><br />I wanted to read this book because i loved the others but this one never caught me in the same way. I even found myself skipping through some bits of the quest. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16440179478771637989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2285707295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6637478009248031681">I'm going to make this a compliment sandwich so this book doesn't feel bad about me not loving it enough.<br/><br/>It was WAY better than the last book.<br/><br/>But the plot is getting stale. Girl meets boy. You're supposed to think they're going to end up together, but they won't. She's end up with the other guy who she butts heads with at the beginning of the book. This is basically the plot of books 1, 2, and 4 (so far). 3 was a little different with less romance. It's getting boring. Also, <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I <s>li</s></span></span>
  <span id="freeText6637478009248031681" style="display:none">I'm going to make this a compliment sandwich so this book doesn't feel bad about me not loving it enough.<br /><br />It was WAY better than the last book.<br /><br />But the plot is getting stale. Girl meets boy. You're supposed to think they're going to end up together, but they won't. She's end up with the other guy who she butts heads with at the beginning of the book. This is basically the plot of books 1, 2, and 4 (so far). 3 was a little different with less romance. It's getting boring. Also, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I <s>liked</s> hated how they got rid of the original love interest. Since he wasn't the villian JM needed a more convenient and less messy way for our heroine to drop him without looking like the bad guy, so she just killed him off. In the most wasteful and stupid way possible. It wasn't even a worthy death that did anything to further the plot. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But the characters were ok and kind of likable. If this was the first in the series I read I might have liked it more, but since I've read 4 of these, I'm kind of over it.</span>

    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ytRRrDBYjBFNyBcsTJeDwV65krdZoONIRxc8d72mvy8k3zcp2KSisliirB4OisFUhfChrA7nPsO5rPOWLMWkBA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3Bqtmn9da6Sko9MbAaYSrNTJa/cohkS3Itnn4a/D6kcyEcsfl6FFB7HJaClDu1A5D4BY7H/BmTzcYigAPqDxbA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier">About Juliet Marillier</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9846408393176522786">Juliet Marillier was born in Dunedin, New Zealand and grew up surrounded by Celtic music and stories. Her own Celtic-Gaelic roots inspired her to write her first series, the Sevenwaters Trilogy. Juliet was educated at the University of Otago, where she majored in music and languages, graduating BA and Bachelor of Music (Hons). Her lifelong interest in history, folklore and mythology has had a majo</span>
  <span id="freeText9846408393176522786" style="display:none">Juliet Marillier was born in Dunedin, New Zealand and grew up surrounded by Celtic music and stories. Her own Celtic-Gaelic roots inspired her to write her first series, the Sevenwaters Trilogy. Juliet was educated at the University of Otago, where she majored in music and languages, graduating BA and Bachelor of Music (Hons). Her lifelong interest in history, folklore and mythology has had a major influence on her writing.<br /><br />Juliet is the author of twenty-one historical fantasy novels for adults and young adults, as well as a book of short fiction. Juliet's novels and short stories have won many awards. <br /><br />Juliet lives in a 110 year old cottage in a riverside suburb of Perth, Western Australia. When not writing, she tends to her small pack of rescue dogs. She also has four adult children and eight grandchildren. Juliet is a member of the druid order OBOD (the Order of Bards, Ovates and Druids.)<br /></span>
